	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">African Union</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>

<p>The <b>African Union</b> (<b>AU</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Continental_union" title="Continental union">continental union</a> consisting of 55 <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_African_Union" title="Member states of the African Union">member states</a> located on the continent of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, with exception of various territories of European possessions located in Africa. The AU was announced in the <a href="/wiki/Sirte_Declaration" title="Sirte Declaration">Sirte Declaration</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sirte_District" title="Sirte District">Sirte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> on 9 September 1999, calling for the establishment of the African Union. The bloc was founded on 26 May 2001 in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> and launched on 9 July 2002 in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-African_Union_2002_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-African_Union_2002-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The intention of the AU is to replace the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_African_Unity" title="Organisation of African Unity">Organisation of African Unity</a> (OAU), established on 25 May 1963 in Addis Ababa by 32 signatory governments. The most important decisions of the AU are made by the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_African_Union" title="Assembly of the African Union">Assembly of the African Union</a>, a semi-annual meeting of the heads of state and government of its member states. The AU's secretariat, the <a href="/wiki/African_Union_Commission" title="African Union Commission">African Union Commission</a>, is based in Addis Ababa.
</p><p>The African Union has just over 1 billion people and an area of around 29&#160;million&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (11&#160;million&#160;sq&#160;mi) and includes popular world landmarks, including the Sahara and the Nile.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The primary languages spoken include <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Africa" title="Languages of Africa">languages of Africa</a>. Within the African Union, there are official bodies such as the <a href="/wiki/Peace_and_Security_Council" title="Peace and Security Council">Peace and Security Council</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pan-African_Parliament" title="Pan-African Parliament">Pan-African Parliament</a>.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The objectives of the AU are the following:
</p>
<ol><li>To achieve greater unity, cohesion and solidarity between the African countries and African nations.</li>
<li>To defend the sovereignty, <a href="/wiki/Territorial_integrity" title="Territorial integrity">territorial integrity</a> and independence of its Member States.</li>
<li>To accelerate the political and social-economic integration of the continent.</li>
<li>To promote and defend African common positions on issues of interest to the continent and its peoples.</li>
<li>To encourage international cooperation, taking due account of the <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_United_Nations" title="Charter of the United Nations">Charter of the United Nations</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a>.</li>
<li>To promote peace, security, and stability on the continent.</li>
<li>To promote democratic principles and institutions, popular participation and good governance.</li>
<li>To promote and protect human and peoples' rights in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/African_Charter_on_Human_and_Peoples%27_Rights" title="African Charter on Human and Peoples&#39; Rights">African Charter on Human and Peoples' Rights</a> and other relevant <a href="/wiki/International_human_rights_instruments" title="International human rights instruments">human rights instruments</a>.</li>
<li>To establish the necessary conditions which enable the continent to play its rightful role in the global economy and in international negotiations.</li>
<li>To promote <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Economic,_social_and_cultural_rights" title="Economic, social and cultural rights">economic, social and cultural levels</a> as well as the integration of African economies.</li>
<li>To promote co-operation in all fields of human activity to raise the <a href="/wiki/Living_standard" class="mw-redirect" title="Living standard">living standards</a> of African peoples.</li>
<li>To coordinate and harmonise the policies between the existing and future <a href="/wiki/Regional_Economic_Communities" title="Regional Economic Communities">Regional Economic Communities</a> for the gradual attainment of the objectives of the Union.</li>
<li>To advance the development of the continent by promoting research in all fields, in particular in science and technology.</li>
<li>To work with relevant international partners in the eradication of preventable diseases and the promotion of good health on the continent.</li></ol>
<p>The African Union is made up of both political and administrative bodies. The highest decision-making organ is the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_African_Union" title="Assembly of the African Union">Assembly of the African Union</a>, made up of all the heads of state or government of member states of the AU. The Assembly is chaired by <a href="/wiki/Abdel_Fattah_el-Sisi" title="Abdel Fattah el-Sisi">Abdel Fattah el-Sisi</a>, President of <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>. The AU also has a representative body, the <a href="/wiki/Pan_African_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan African Parliament">Pan African Parliament</a>, which consists of 265 members elected by the national legislatures of the AU member states. Its president is <a href="/wiki/Roger_Nkodo_Dang" title="Roger Nkodo Dang">Roger Nkodo Dang</a>.
</p><p>Other political institutions of the AU include:
</p>
<ul><li>the <a href="/wiki/Executive_Council_of_the_African_Union" title="Executive Council of the African Union">Executive Council</a>, made up of <a href="/wiki/Foreign_minister" title="Foreign minister">foreign ministers</a>, which prepares decisions for the Assembly;</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Representatives%27_Committee_of_the_African_Union" title="Permanent Representatives&#39; Committee of the African Union">Permanent Representatives Committee</a>, made up of the ambassadors to <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a> of AU member states; and</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Economic,_Social,_and_Cultural_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic, Social, and Cultural Council">Economic, Social, and Cultural Council</a> (ECOSOCC), a civil society consultative body.</li></ul>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/African_Union_Commission" title="African Union Commission">AU Commission</a>, the secretariat to the political structures, is chaired by <a href="/wiki/Nkosazana_Dlamini-Zuma" title="Nkosazana Dlamini-Zuma">Nkosazana Dlamini-Zuma</a> of South Africa. On 15 July 2012, Ms. Dlamini-Zuma won a tightly contested vote to become the first female head of the African Union Commission, replacing <a href="/wiki/Jean_Ping" title="Jean Ping">Jean Ping</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>.
</p><p>Other AU structures are hosted by different member states:
</p>
<ul><li>the <a href="/wiki/African_Commission_on_Human_and_Peoples%27_Rights" title="African Commission on Human and Peoples&#39; Rights">African Commission on Human and Peoples' Rights</a> is based in <a href="/wiki/Banjul" title="Banjul">Banjul</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Gambia" title="The Gambia">the Gambia</a>; and</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/New_Partnership_for_Africa%27s_Development" title="New Partnership for Africa&#39;s Development">New Partnership for Africa's Development</a> (NEPAD) and <a href="/wiki/APRM" class="mw-redirect" title="APRM">APRM</a> <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/secretariat" class="extiw" title="wikt:secretariat">Secretariats</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pan-African_Parliament" title="Pan-African Parliament">Pan-African Parliament</a> are in <a href="/wiki/Midrand" title="Midrand">Midrand</a>, South Africa.</li></ul>
<p>The AU's first military intervention in a member state was the May 2003 deployment of a peacekeeping force of soldiers from South Africa, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> to <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a> to oversee the implementation of the various agreements. AU troops were also deployed in <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> for peacekeeping during <a href="/wiki/Darfur_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Darfur conflict">Darfur conflict</a>, before the mission was handed over to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> on 1 January 2008 <a href="/wiki/UNAMID" class="mw-redirect" title="UNAMID">UNAMID</a>. The AU has also sent a peacekeeping mission to <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, of which the peacekeeping troops are from <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> and Burundi.
</p><p>The AU has adopted a number of important new documents establishing norms at continental level, to supplement those already in force when it was created. These include the <a href="/wiki/African_Union_Convention_on_Preventing_and_Combating_Corruption" title="African Union Convention on Preventing and Combating Corruption">African Union Convention on Preventing and Combating Corruption</a> (2003), the <a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Charter_on_Democracy,_Elections_and_Governance&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="African Charter on Democracy, Elections and Governance (page does not exist)">African Charter on Democracy, Elections and Governance</a> (2007), the <a href="/wiki/New_Partnership_for_Africa%27s_Development" title="New Partnership for Africa&#39;s Development">New Partnership for Africa's Development</a> (NEPAD) and its associated Declaration on Democracy, Political, Economic and Corporate Governance.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_African_Union" title="History of the African Union">History of the African Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Africa" title="History of Africa">History of Africa</a></div>
<p>The historical foundations of the African Union originated in the <b>First Congress of Independence African States</b>, held in <a href="/wiki/Accra" title="Accra">Accra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>, from 15 to 22 April 1958. The conference aimed at forming the <a href="/wiki/Africa_Day" title="Africa Day">Africa Day</a>, to mark the liberation movement each year concerning the willingness of the African people to free themselves from foreign dictatorship, as well as subsequent attempts to unite Africa, including the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_African_Unity" title="Organisation of African Unity">Organisation of African Unity</a> (OAU), which was established on 25 May 1963, and the <a href="/wiki/African_Economic_Community" title="African Economic Community">African Economic Community</a> in 1981.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
Critics argued that the OAU in particular did little to protect the rights and liberties of African citizens from their own political leaders, often dubbing it the "Dictators' Club".<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The idea of creating the AU was revived in the mid-1990s under the leadership of Libyan head of state <a href="/wiki/Muammar_al-Gaddafi" class="mw-redirect" title="Muammar al-Gaddafi">Muammar al-Gaddafi</a>: the heads of state and government of the OAU issued the <a href="/wiki/Sirte_Declaration" title="Sirte Declaration">Sirte Declaration</a> (named after Sirte, in Libya) on 9 September 1999, calling for the establishment of an African Union. The Declaration was followed by summits at <a href="/wiki/Lom%C3%A9" title="Lomé">Lomé</a> in 2000, when the <a href="/wiki/Constitutive_Act_of_the_African_Union" title="Constitutive Act of the African Union">Constitutive Act of the African Union</a> was adopted, and at <a href="/wiki/Lusaka" title="Lusaka">Lusaka</a> in 2001, when the plan for the implementation of the African Union was adopted. During the same period, the initiative for the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/New_Partnership_for_Africa%27s_Development" title="New Partnership for Africa&#39;s Development">New Partnership for Africa's Development</a> (NEPAD), was also established.
</p><p>The African Union was launched in <a href="/wiki/Durban" title="Durban">Durban</a> on 9 July 2002, by its first chairperson, South African <a href="/wiki/Thabo_Mbeki" title="Thabo Mbeki">Thabo Mbeki</a>, at the first session of the Assembly of the African Union. The second session of the Assembly was in <a href="/wiki/Maputo" title="Maputo">Maputo</a> in 2003, and the third session in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a> on 6 July 2004.
</p><p>Since 2010, the African Union eyes the establishment of a joint African <a href="/wiki/Space_agency" class="mw-redirect" title="Space agency">space agency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> was the first ever sitting <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> president to speak in front of the African Union in Addis Ababa, on 29 July 2015. With his speech, he encouraged the world to increase economic ties via investments and trade with the <a href="/wiki/Outline_of_Africa" title="Outline of Africa">continent</a>, and lauded the progresses made in <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Africa" title="Education in Africa">education</a>, infrastructure and <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Africa" title="Economy of Africa">economy</a>. But he also criticised a lack of democracy and leaders who refuse to step down, discrimination against minorities (including <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> people, religious groups and ethnicities) and corruption. He suggested an intensified <a href="/wiki/Democratisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratisation">democratisation</a> and free trade, to significantly increase living quality for Africans.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_African_Union" title="Geography of the African Union">Geography of the African Union</a></div>
<p>Member <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">states</a> of the African Union cover almost the entirety of continental Africa, except for several territories held by <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> (<a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plazas_de_soberan%C3%ADa" title="Plazas de soberanía">Plazas de soberanía</a>); <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="Réunion">Réunion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scattered_Islands_in_the_Indian_Ocean" title="Scattered Islands in the Indian Ocean">Scattered Islands in the Indian Ocean</a>); Portugal (<a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Savage_Islands" title="Savage Islands">Savage Islands</a>); and the United Kingdom (<a href="/wiki/Saint_Helena,_Ascension_and_Tristan_da_Cunha" title="Saint Helena, Ascension and Tristan da Cunha">Saint Helena, Ascension and Tristan da Cunha</a>). Consequently, the geography of the African Union is wildly diverse, including the world's largest hot desert (the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>), huge jungles and <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savannas</a>, and the world's longest river (the <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a>).
</p><p>The AU presently has an area of 29,922,059 square kilometres (11,552,972&#160;sq&#160;mi), with 24,165 kilometres (15,015&#160;mi) of coastline. The vast majority of this area is on continental Africa, while the only significant territory off the mainland is the island of <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> (<a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_area" title="List of islands by area">the world's fourth largest island</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Sinai_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Sinai peninsula">Sinai peninsula</a> accounting for slightly less than 2% of the total.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Africa" title="Demographics of Africa">Demographics of Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_African_Union" title="Member states of the African Union">Member states of the African Union</a></div>
<p>Total population of the African Union as of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> is estimated at more than 1.25 billion, with a growth rate of more than 2.5% p.a.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_African_Union" title="Languages of the African Union">Languages of the African Union</a></div>
<p>According to the Constitutive Act of the African Union, its working languages are Arabic, English, French and Portuguese, and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Africa" title="Languages of Africa">African languages</a> "if possible".<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> A protocol amending the Constitutive Act, adopted in 2003 but as of June 2016 not yet ratified by a two-thirds majority of member states, would add Spanish, <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a> and "any other African language" and declare all "official" (rather than "working") languages of the African Union.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The Executive Council shall determine the process and practical modalities for the use of official languages as working languages.
</p><p>Founded in 2001 under the auspices of the AU, the <a href="/wiki/African_Academy_of_Languages" title="African Academy of Languages">African Academy of Languages</a> promotes the usage and perpetuation of <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Africa" title="Languages of Africa">African</a> languages among African people. The AU declared 2006 the Year of African Languages.<sup id="cite_ref-Year_of_African_Languages_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Year_of_African_Languages-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Year_of_African_Languages_2_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Year_of_African_Languages_2-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> 2006 also marked Ghana's 55th anniversary since it founded the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Ghana_Languages" title="Bureau of Ghana Languages">Bureau of Ghana Languages</a> originally known as <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Ghana_Languages" title="Bureau of Ghana Languages">Gold Coast Vernacular Literature Bureau</a>.
</p>

<p>The African Union has a number of official bodies:
</p>
<dl><dt><a href="/wiki/Pan-African_Parliament" title="Pan-African Parliament">Pan-African Parliament</a> (PAP)</dt>
<dd>To become the highest legislative body of the African Union. The seat of the PAP is at <a href="/wiki/Midrand" title="Midrand">Midrand</a>, South Africa. The Parliament is composed of 265&#160;elected representatives from all 55&#160;AU states, and intended to provide popular and civil-society participation in the processes of democratic governance. Its president is <a href="/wiki/Roger_Nkodo_Dang" title="Roger Nkodo Dang">Roger Nkodo Dang</a>, of <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_African_Union" title="Assembly of the African Union">Assembly of the African Union</a></dt>
<dd>Composed of heads of state and heads of government of AU states, the Assembly is currently the supreme governing body of the African Union. It is gradually devolving some of its decision-making powers to the Pan African Parliament. It meets once a year and makes its decisions by consensus or by a two-thirds majority. The current <a href="/wiki/Chairperson_of_the_African_Union" title="Chairperson of the African Union">chair of the AU</a> is <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egyptian</a> President <a href="/wiki/Abdel_Fattah_el-Sisi" title="Abdel Fattah el-Sisi">Abdel Fattah el-Sisi</a>.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/African_Union_Commission" title="African Union Commission">African Union Commission (or Authority)</a>&#160;</dt>
<dd>The secretariat of the African Union, composed of ten commissioners and supporting staff and headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>, Ethiopia. In a similar fashion to its <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European</a> counterpart, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, it is responsible for the administration and co-ordination of the AU's activities and meetings.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Court_of_Justice_of_the_African_Union" title="Court of Justice of the African Union">Court of Justice of the African Union</a></dt>
<dd>The Constitutive Act provides for a Court of Justice to rule on disputes over interpretation of AU treaties. A protocol to set up this Court of Justice was adopted in 2003 and entered into force in 2009. It was, however, superseded by a protocol creating an <a href="/wiki/African_Court_of_Justice_and_Human_Rights" title="African Court of Justice and Human Rights">African Court of Justice and Human Rights</a>, which will incorporate the already established <a href="/wiki/African_Court_on_Human_and_Peoples%27_Rights" title="African Court on Human and Peoples&#39; Rights">African Court on Human and Peoples' Rights</a> (see below) and have two chambers: one for general legal matters and one for rulings on the human rights treaties.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Executive_Council_of_the_African_Union" title="Executive Council of the African Union">Executive Council</a></dt>
<dd>Composed of ministers designated by the governments of member states. It decides on matters such as foreign trade, social security, food, agriculture and communications, is accountable to the Assembly, and prepares material for the Assembly to discuss and approve.It is chaired by Mr Shawn Makuyana of Zimbabwe (2015–).</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Permanent_Representatives%27_Committee_of_the_African_Union" title="Permanent Representatives&#39; Committee of the African Union">Permanent Representatives' Committee</a></dt>
<dd>Consisting of nominated permanent representatives of member states, the Committee prepares the work for the Executive Council, similar the role of the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Permanent_Representatives" title="Committee of Permanent Representatives">Committee of Permanent Representatives</a> in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Peace_and_Security_Council" title="Peace and Security Council">Peace and Security Council</a> (PSC)</dt>
<dd>Proposed at the Lusaka Summit in 2001 and established in 2004 under a protocol to the Constitutive Act adopted by the AU Assembly in July 2002. The protocol defines the PSC as a collective security and early warning arrangement to facilitate timely and effective response to conflict and crisis situations in Africa. Other responsibilities conferred to the PSC by the protocol include prevention, management and resolution of conflicts, post-conflict peace building and developing common defence policies. The PSC has fifteen members elected on a regional basis by the Assembly. Similar in intent and operation to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>.</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Economic,_Social_and_Cultural_Council" title="Economic, Social and Cultural Council">Economic, Social and Cultural Council</a></dt>
<dd>An advisory organ composed of professional and civic representatives, similar to the European <a href="/wiki/Economic_and_Social_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic and Social Committee">Economic and Social Committee</a>. The chair of ECOSOCC, elected in 2008, is Cameroonian lawyer <a href="/wiki/Akere_Muna" title="Akere Muna">Akere Muna</a> of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pan-African_Lawyers_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pan-African Lawyers Union (page does not exist)">Pan-African Lawyers Union</a> (PALU).</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Specialised_Technical_Committees_of_the_African_Union" title="Specialised Technical Committees of the African Union">Specialised Technical Committees</a></dt>
<dd>Both the Abuja Treaty and the Constitutive Act provide for Specialised Technical Committees to be established made up of African ministers to advise the Assembly. In practice, they have never been set up. The ten proposed themes are: Rural Economy and Agricultural Matters; Monetary and Financial Affairs; Trade, Customs, and Immigration; Industry, Science and Technology; Energy, Natural Resources, and Environment; Transport, Communications, and Tourism; Health; Labour, and Social Affairs; Education, Culture, and Human Resources.</dd>
<dt>Financial institutions</dt>
<dd></dd></dl>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/African_Central_Bank" title="African Central Bank">African Central Bank</a> – <a href="/wiki/Abuja" title="Abuja">Abuja</a>, Nigeria</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/African_Investment_Bank" title="African Investment Bank">African Investment Bank</a> – <a href="/wiki/Tripoli" title="Tripoli">Tripoli</a>, Libya</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/African_Monetary_Fund" title="African Monetary Fund">African Monetary Fund</a> – <a href="/wiki/Yaound%C3%A9" title="Yaoundé">Yaoundé</a>, Cameroon</li></ul>
<p>These institutions have not yet been established, however, the Steering Committees working on their founding have been constituted. Eventually, the AU aims to have a single currency (the <a href="/wiki/Afro_(currency)" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro (currency)">Afro</a>).
</p>
<dl><dt>Human rights</dt>
<dd>The <a href="/wiki/African_Commission_on_Human_and_Peoples%27_Rights" title="African Commission on Human and Peoples&#39; Rights">African Commission on Human and Peoples' Rights</a>, in existence since 1986, is established under the <a href="/wiki/African_Charter_on_Human_and_Peoples%27_Rights" title="African Charter on Human and Peoples&#39; Rights">African Charter on Human and Peoples' Rights</a> (the African Charter) rather than the Constitutive Act of the African Union. It is the premier African human rights body, with responsibility for monitoring and promoting compliance with the African Charter. The <a href="/wiki/African_Court_on_Human_and_Peoples%27_Rights" title="African Court on Human and Peoples&#39; Rights">African Court on Human and Peoples' Rights</a> was established in 2006 to supplement the work of the Commission, following the entry into force of a protocol to the African Charter providing for its creation. It is planned that the African Court on Human and Peoples' Rights will be merged with the Court of Justice of the African Union (see above).</dd>
<dt><a href="/wiki/African_Energy_Commission" title="African Energy Commission">African Energy Commission</a></dt></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership">Membership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Membership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_African_Union" title="Member states of the African Union">Member states of the African Union</a></div>
<p>All <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">UN member states</a> based in Africa and on African waters are members of the AU, as is the <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_the_Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic" title="International recognition of the Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic">disputed</a> <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic" title="Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic">Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic</a> (SADR). <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, which claims sovereignty over the SADR's territory, withdrew from the Organisation of African Unity, the AU's predecessor, in 1984 due to the admission of the SADR as a member. However, on 30 January 2017, the AU admitted Morocco as a member state.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbulletin_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbulletin-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_the_African_Union.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Regions_of_the_African_Union.png/220px-Regions_of_the_African_Union.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Regions_of_the_African_Union.png/330px-Regions_of_the_African_Union.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Regions_of_the_African_Union.png/440px-Regions_of_the_African_Union.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_the_African_Union.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Regions_of_the_African_Union" title="Regions of the African Union">Regions of the African Union</a>:<br /> <span style="background-color:#DAA520; color:black; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&#160;<b>Northern Region</b>   (Sahara)&#160;</span>, <span style="background-color:#87CEEB; color:black; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&#160;<b>Southern Region</b>   (Kalahari)&#160;</span>, <span style="background-color:#90EE90; color:black; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&#160;<b>Eastern Region</b>  (Nile)&#160;</span>, <span style="background-color:#FA8072; color:black; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&#160;<b>Western Regions A and B</b>  (Niger and Volta Niger)&#160;</span>, <span style="background-color:#B88FFF; color:black; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&#160;<b>Central Region</b> (Congo) &#160;</span></div></div></div>
<p><br />
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The principal topic for debate at the July 2007 AU summit held in <a href="/wiki/Accra" title="Accra">Accra</a>, Ghana, was the creation of a Union Government,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> with the aim of moving towards a <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_Africa" title="United States of Africa">United States of Africa</a>. A study on the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Government_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Union Government of Africa (page does not exist)">Union Government</a> was adopted in late 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> and proposes various options for "completing" the African Union project. There are divisions among African states on the proposals, with some (notably <a href="/wiki/Great_Socialist_People%27s_Libyan_Arab_Jamahiriya" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Socialist People&#39;s Libyan Arab Jamahiriya">Libya</a>) following a maximalist view leading to a common government with an AU army; and others (especially the southern African states) supporting rather a strengthening of the existing structures, with some reforms to deal with administrative and political challenges in making the AU Commission and other bodies truly effective.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following a heated debate in Accra, the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_African_Union" title="Assembly of the African Union">Assembly of Heads of State and Government</a> agreed in the form of a declaration to review the state of affairs of the AU with a view to determining its readiness towards a Union Government.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In particular, the Assembly agreed to:
</p>
<ul><li>Accelerate the economic and political integration of the African continent, including the formation of a <a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Government_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Union Government of Africa (page does not exist)">Union Government of Africa</a>;</li>
<li>Conduct an audit of the institutions and organs of the AU; review the relationship between the AU and the RECs; find ways to strengthen the AU and elaborate a timeframe to establish a Union Government of Africa.</li></ul>
<p>The declaration lastly noted the "importance of involving the African peoples, including Africans in the Diaspora, in the processes leading to the formation of the Union Government."
</p><p>Following this decision, a panel of eminent persons was set up to conduct the "audit review". The review team began its work on 1 September 2007. The review was presented to the Assembly of Heads of State and Government at the January 2008 summit in Addis Ababa. No final decision was taken on the recommendations, however, and a committee of ten heads of state was appointed to consider the review and report back to the July 2008 summit to be held in Egypt.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> At the July 2008 summit, a decision was once again deferred, for a "final" debate at the January 2009 summit to be held in Addis Ababa.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Role_of_African_Union">Role of African Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Role of African Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<p>One of the key debates in relation to the achievement of greater continental integration is the relative priority that should be given to integration of the continent as a unit in itself or to integration of the sub-regions. The 1980 <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Plan_of_Action_for_the_Development_of_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Lagos Plan of Action for the Development of Africa">Lagos Plan of Action for the Development of Africa</a> and the 1991 treaty to establish the African Economic Community (also referred to as the Abuja Treaty), proposed the creation of <a href="/wiki/Regional_Economic_Communities" title="Regional Economic Communities">Regional Economic Communities</a> (RECs) as the basis for African integration, with a timetable for regional and then continental integration to follow.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Currently, there are eight RECs recognised by the AU, each established under a separate regional treaty. They are:
</p>
<ul><li>the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Maghreb_Union" title="Arab Maghreb Union">Arab Maghreb Union</a> (AMU)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Common_Market_for_Eastern_and_Southern_Africa" title="Common Market for Eastern and Southern Africa">Common Market for Eastern and Southern Africa</a> (COMESA)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Sahel-Saharan_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Community of Sahel-Saharan States">Community of Sahel-Saharan States</a> (CEN-SAD)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a> (EAC)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_Central_African_States" title="Economic Community of Central African States">Economic Community of Central African States</a> (ECCAS)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a> (ECOWAS)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Authority_on_Development" title="Intergovernmental Authority on Development">Intergovernmental Authority on Development</a> (IGAD)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa_Development_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Africa Development Community">Southern Africa Development Community</a> (SADC)</li></ul>
<p>The membership of many of the communities overlaps, and their rationalisation has been under discussion for several years—and formed the theme of the 2006 Banjul summit. At the July 2007 Accra summit the Assembly finally decided to adopt a Protocol on Relations between the African Union and the Regional Economic Communities.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> This protocol is intended to facilitate the harmonisation of policies and ensure compliance with the Abuja Treaty and Lagos Plan of Action time frames.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Selection_of_chair">Selection of chair</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Selection of chair">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2006, the AU decided to create a Committee "to consider the implementation of a rotation system between the regions" in relation to the presidency. Controversy arose at the 2006 summit when Sudan announced its candidacy for the AU's chairmanship, as a representative of the East African region. Several member states refused to support Sudan because of tensions over <a href="/wiki/Darfur" title="Darfur">Darfur</a> (see also below). Sudan ultimately withdrew its candidacy and President <a href="/wiki/Denis_Sassou-Nguesso" class="mw-redirect" title="Denis Sassou-Nguesso">Denis Sassou-Nguesso</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> was elected to a one-year term. At the January 2007 summit, Sassou-Nguesso was replaced by President <a href="/wiki/John_Agyekum_Kufuor" class="mw-redirect" title="John Agyekum Kufuor">John Agyekum Kufuor</a> of Ghana, despite another attempt by Sudan to gain the chair. 2007 was the 50th anniversary of Ghana's independence, a symbolic moment for the country to hold the chair of the AU—and to host the mid-year summit at which the proposed Union Government was also discussed. In January 2008, President <a href="/wiki/Jakaya_Kikwete" title="Jakaya Kikwete">Jakaya Kikwete</a> of Tanzania took over as chair, representing the East African region and thus apparently ending Sudan's attempt to become chair—at least till the rotation returns to East Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The current chair is Egypt.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Headquarters">Headquarters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Headquarters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:African_Union_conference_center_and_office_complex,_AUCC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/African_Union_conference_center_and_office_complex%2C_AUCC.jpg/250px-African_Union_conference_center_and_office_complex%2C_AUCC.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/African_Union_conference_center_and_office_complex%2C_AUCC.jpg/375px-African_Union_conference_center_and_office_complex%2C_AUCC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/African_Union_conference_center_and_office_complex%2C_AUCC.jpg/500px-African_Union_conference_center_and_office_complex%2C_AUCC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2686" data-file-height="1988" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:African_Union_conference_center_and_office_complex,_AUCC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/AU_Conference_Center_and_Office_Complex" title="AU Conference Center and Office Complex">AU Conference Center and Office Complex</a>, the African Union's headquarters complex in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a></div></div></div>
<p>The main administrative capital of the African Union is in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, where the African Union Commission is headquartered. A new headquarters complex, the <a href="/wiki/AU_Conference_Center_and_Office_Complex" title="AU Conference Center and Office Complex">AU Conference Center and Office Complex</a> (AUCC), was inaugurated on 28 January 2012, during the 18th AU summit.<sup id="cite_ref-AU_NewHQ_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AU_NewHQ-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The complex was built by <a href="/wiki/China_State_Construction_Engineering_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="China State Construction Engineering Corporation">China State Construction Engineering Corporation</a> as a gift from the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of the People&#39;s Republic of China">Chinese government</a>, and accommodates, among other facilities, a 2,500-seat plenary hall and a 20-story office tower. The tower is 99.9 meters high to signify the date 9 September 1999, when the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_African_Unity" title="Organisation of African Unity">Organisation of African Unity</a> voted to become the African Union.<sup id="cite_ref-Chinadaily_NewHQ_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chinadaily_NewHQ-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The building cost US$200 million to construct.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 26 January 2018, five years after the building's completion, the French Newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Monde" title="Le Monde">Le Monde</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> published an article stating that the Chinese government had heavily bugged the building, installing listening devices in the walls and furniture and setting up the computer system to copy data to servers in Shanghai daily.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The Chinese government denied that they bugged the building, stating that the accusations were "utterly groundless and ridiculous."<sup id="cite_ref-:1_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Ethiopian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Hailemariam_Desalegn" title="Hailemariam Desalegn">Hailemariam Desalegn</a> rejected the French media report.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Moussa_Faki" title="Moussa Faki">Moussa Faki Mahamat</a>, head of the African Union Commission, said the allegations in the Le Monde's report were false. "These are totally false allegations and I believe that we are completely disregarding them."<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_African_Union" title="Foreign relations of the African Union">Foreign relations of the African Union</a></div>
<p>The individual member states of the African Union coordinate foreign policy through this agency, in addition to conducting their own <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international relations</a> on a state-by-state basis. The AU represents the interests of African peoples at large in <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Intergovernmental organisation">intergovernmental organisations</a> (IGOs); for instance, it is a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">permanent observer</a> at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a>. Both the African Union and the United Nations work in tandem to address issues of common concerns in various areas. The African Union Mission in United Nations aspires to serve as a bridge between the two Organisations.
</p><p>Membership of the AU overlaps with other IGOs and occasionally these third-party organisations and the AU will coordinate matters of public policy. The African Union maintains special diplomatic representation with the <a href="/wiki/Ambassadors_from_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Ambassadors from the United States">United States</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Special_Representative" title="European Union Special Representative">European Union</a>.
</p><p>In 2016, the Union introduced continent-wide passports.<sup id="cite_ref-passport_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-passport-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Upon the election of Donald Trump for the presidency of the U.S., in 2017, the latter passed an executive order for a ban on citizens from seven countries with suspected links to terrorism, that concerns three African countries. During the 28th African Union Summit, in Ethiopia, African leaders criticised the ban<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> as they expressed their growing concerns for the African Economy, under Trump's policies.
</p>
<h3><span id="Africa.E2.80.93China_relations"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa–China_relations">Africa–China relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Africa–China relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Africa%E2%80%93China_relations" title="Africa–China relations">Africa–China relations</a></div>
<p>One of the leading economic partners of the continent has been the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a> (PRC). In September 2018, the bloc held its third <a href="/wiki/Forum_on_China%E2%80%93Africa_Cooperation" title="Forum on China–Africa Cooperation">Forum on China–Africa Cooperation</a> summit in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, China.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_African_Union" title="Economy of the African Union">Economy of the African Union</a></div>
<p>The AU's future goals include the creation of a <a href="/wiki/African_Continental_Free_Trade_Area" title="African Continental Free Trade Area">free trade area</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Customs_union" title="Customs union">customs union</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Single_market" title="Single market">single market</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a>, and a common currency (see <a href="/wiki/African_Monetary_Union" title="African Monetary Union">African Monetary Union</a>), thereby establishing <a href="/wiki/Economic_and_monetary_union" title="Economic and monetary union">economic and monetary union</a>. The current plan is to establish an <a href="/wiki/African_Economic_Community" title="African Economic Community">African Economic Community</a> with a single currency by 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indicators">Indicators</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Indicators">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
