<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">Symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Emblem_of_the_African_Union.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Emblem_of_the_African_Union.svg/200px-Emblem_of_the_African_Union.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Emblem_of_the_African_Union.svg/300px-Emblem_of_the_African_Union.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Emblem_of_the_African_Union.svg/400px-Emblem_of_the_African_Union.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="145" data-file-height="130" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Emblem_of_the_African_Union.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Emblem of the African Union</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Emblem_of_the_African_Union" title="Emblem of the African Union">emblem of the African Union</a> consists of a gold ribbon bearing small interlocking red rings, from which palm leaves shoot up around an outer gold circle and an inner green circle, within which is a gold representation of Africa. The red interlinked rings stand for African solidarity and the blood shed for the liberation of Africa; the palm leaves for peace; the gold, for Africa's wealth and bright future; the green, for African hopes and aspirations. To symbolise African unity, the silhouette of Africa is drawn without internal borders.
</p><p>The African Union adopted its new flag at its 14th Ordinary Session of the Assembly of Heads of State and Government taking place in Addis Ababa 2010. During the 8th African Union Summit which took place in Addis Ababa on 29 and 30 January 2007, the Heads of State and Government decided to launch a competition for the selection of a new flag for the Union. They prescribed a green background for the flag symbolising hope of Africa and stars to represent Member States.
</p><p>Pursuant to this decision, the African Union Commission (AUC) organised a competition for the selection of a new flag for the African Union. The AUC received a total of 106 entries proposed by citizens of 19 African countries and 2 from the Diaspora. The proposals were then examined by a panel of experts put in place by the African Union Commission and selected from the five African regions for short listing according to the main directions given by the Heads of State and Government.
</p><p>At the 13th Ordinary Session of the Assembly, the Heads of State and Government examined the report of the Panel and selected one among all the proposals. The flag is now part of the paraphernalia of the African Union and replaces the old one.
</p><p>The old <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_African_Union" title="Flag of the African Union">flag of the African Union</a> bears a broad green horizontal stripe, a narrow band of gold, the emblem of the African Union at the centre of a broad white stripe, another narrow gold band and a final broad green stripe. Again, the green and gold symbolise Africa's hopes and aspirations as well as its wealth and bright future, and the white represents the purity of Africa's desire for friends throughout the world. The flag has led to the creation of the "<a href="/wiki/National_colours" title="National colours">national colours</a>" of Africa of gold and green (sometimes together with white). These colours are visible in one way or another in the flags of many African nations. Together the colours green, gold, and red constitute the <a href="/wiki/Pan-African_colours" title="Pan-African colours">Pan-African colours</a>.
</p><p>The African Union has adopted the anthem, "<a href="/wiki/Let_Us_All_Unite_and_Celebrate_Together" title="Let Us All Unite and Celebrate Together">Let Us All Unite and Celebrate Together</a>".
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Celebration">Celebration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Celebration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Africa_Day" title="Africa Day">Africa Day</a>, formerly African Freedom Day and African Liberation Day, is an annual commemoration regarding the founding of the Organisation of African Unity (OAU), on 25 May 1963, and occurring on the same date of the month each year. Other celebrations include the following:
</p>
<ul><li>The Fez Festival of World Sacred Music: a week long celebration for harmony between cultures with dancing, Moroccan music, art exhibitions and films.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The Knysna <a href="/wiki/Oyster_festival" title="Oyster festival">Oyster festival</a>: held in <a href="/wiki/Knysna" title="Knysna">Knysna</a> and focused around sport, food and their oyster heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lake_of_Stars_Festival" title="Lake of Stars Festival">Lake of Stars Festival</a>: three-day celebration that takes place in <a href="/wiki/Lake_Malawi" title="Lake Malawi">Lake Malawi</a>, showcasing African music and welcoming people from around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/F%C3%AAte_du_Vodoun" title="Fête du Vodoun">Fête du Vodoun</a>: also known as the Ouidah Voodoo Festival. It is centred around their rituals on voodoo temples, with entertainment that includes horse races and traditional drum performances.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Umhlanga_(ceremony)" title="Umhlanga (ceremony)">Umhlanga (ceremony)</a>: is mainly a private event for young women but on the sixth and seventh days the traditions are done publicly.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Marsabit Lake Turkana Cultural Festival: held in Kenya and celebrates harmony amongst tribes with their culture, singing, dancing and traditional costumes.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_issues">Current issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Current issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The AU faces many challenges, including health issues such as combating <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> and the <a href="/wiki/AIDS/HIV" class="mw-redirect" title="AIDS/HIV">AIDS/HIV</a> epidemic; political issues such as confronting undemocratic regimes and mediating in the many civil wars; economic issues such as improving the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">standard of living</a> of millions of impoverished, uneducated Africans; ecological issues such as dealing with recurring famines, <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a>, and lack of ecological <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainability</a>; as well as the <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">legal</a> <a href="/wiki/Legal_status_of_Western_Sahara" class="mw-redirect" title="Legal status of Western Sahara">issues regarding Western Sahara</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="AIDS_in_Africa">AIDS in Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: AIDS in Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The AU has been active in addressing the AIDS pandemic in Africa. In 2001, the AU established AIDS Watch Africa to coordinate and mobilise a continent-wide response.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>, especially southern and eastern Africa, is the most affected area in the world. Though this region is home to only 6.2% of the world's population, it is also home to half of the world's population infected with HIV.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> While the measurement of HIV prevalence rates has proved methodologically challenging, more than 20% of the sexually active population of many countries of southern Africa may be infected, with South Africa, Botswana, <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, Namibia, and <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> all expected to have a decrease in <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> by an average of 6.5 years. The pandemic has had massive implications for the economy of the continent, reducing economic growth rates by 2–4% across Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2007, the AU endorsed two new initiatives to combat the AIDS crisis, including a push to recruit, train and integrate 2 million community health workers into the continent's healthcare systems.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2012, the African Union Assembly requested that the African Union Commission would work out “a roadmap of shared responsibility to draw on African efforts for a viable health funding with support of traditional and emerging partners to address AIDS dependency response.” Once created, the roadmap (as it is officially known) provided a group of solutions that would enhance the shared responsibility and global solidarity for <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">AIDS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">TB</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">Malaria</a> responses in Africa by 2015. The roadmap was organised into three pillars which were: diversified financing, access to medicines, and enhanced health governance. The roadmap held stakeholders accountable for the realisation of these solutions between 2012 and 2015.
</p><p>The first pillar, diversified financing, ensures that countries begin to develop a country specific financial sustainability plans with clear targets, and identify and maximise opportunities to diversify funding sources in order to increase the domestic resource allocation to AIDS and other diseases.
</p><p>The second pillar, access to affordable and quality-assured medicines, tries to promote and facilitate investing in leading medicine hub manufacturers in Africa, accelerate and strengthen medicine regulatory harmonisation, and create legislation that would help to protect the knowledge of the researchers who develop these life-saving medicines.
</p><p>The third pillar, enhanced leadership and governance, tries to invest in programs that support people and communities to prevent HIV and ensure that leadership at all levels is mobilised to implement the roadmap. There are several organisations that will ensure the smooth implementation of the roadmap, including <a href="/wiki/New_Partnership_for_Africa%27s_Development" title="New Partnership for Africa&#39;s Development">NEPAD</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joint_United_Nations_Programme_on_HIV/AIDS" title="Joint United Nations Programme on HIV/AIDS">UNAIDS</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">WHO</a>, and several other UN partners.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption">Corruption</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Corruption">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Daniel Batidam, an anti-corruption advisory board member of the African Union, resigned after stating that the organisation had "multiple irregularities" and that "issues have come up over and over again" regarding corruption. The African Union quickly accepted his resignation, with Batidam saying that it was a sign that mismanagement towards corruption will "continue with business as usual".<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libya">Libya</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Libya">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When the conflicts in Libya began in 2011, the African Union was initially criticised for not doing much to prevent the escalation of conflict in Libya. Additionally, the AU hesitated to take a side when the conflict in Libya began. There was some vagueness when it came to the African Union's position in the conflict, it was unclear if they were fully supporting the Libyan regime or if they were instead supporting the Libyan citizens. This ambiguity occurred right around the time when there were several human right violations against the Libyan regime. It was later realised that the hesitation in the AU's response to the Arab Spring in Libya was due to its lack of capacity and capability for engaging in democratic reforms.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The AU attempted to mediate in the early stages of the <a href="/wiki/2011_Libyan_civil_war" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Libyan civil war">2011 Libyan civil war</a>, forming an <i>ad hoc</i> committee of five presidents (<a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Congolese</a> President <a href="/wiki/Denis_Sassou_Nguesso" title="Denis Sassou Nguesso">Denis Sassou Nguesso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Malian</a> President <a href="/wiki/Amadou_Toumani_Tour%C3%A9" title="Amadou Toumani Touré">Amadou Toumani Touré</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritanian</a> President <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Ould_Abdel_Aziz" title="Mohamed Ould Abdel Aziz">Mohamed Ould Abdel Aziz</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South African</a> President <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Zuma" title="Jacob Zuma">Jacob Zuma</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Ugandan</a> President <a href="/wiki/Yoweri_Museveni" title="Yoweri Museveni">Yoweri Museveni</a>) to broker a truce.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> However, the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>-led <a href="/wiki/2011_military_intervention_in_Libya" title="2011 military intervention in Libya">military intervention</a> in March 2011 prevented the committee from traveling to <a href="/wiki/Great_Socialist_People%27s_Libyan_Arab_Jamahiriya" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Socialist People&#39;s Libyan Arab Jamahiriya">Libya</a> to meet with Libyan leader and former head of the AU until 2010 <a href="/wiki/Muammar_Gaddafi" title="Muammar Gaddafi">Muammar Gaddafi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> As a body, the AU sharply dissented from the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>'s decision to create a <a href="/wiki/No-fly_zone" title="No-fly zone">no-fly zone</a> over Libya,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> though a few member states, such as <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> and others expressed support for <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1973" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1973">the resolution</a>.
</p><p>As a result of Gaddafi's defeat at the <a href="/wiki/2011_Battle_of_Tripoli" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Battle of Tripoli">Battle of Tripoli</a>, the decisive battle of the war, in August 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a> voted to recognise the anti-Gaddafi <a href="/wiki/National_Transitional_Council" title="National Transitional Council">National Transitional Council</a> as the legitimate government of the country pending elections,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> yet although the council has been recognised by several AU member states, including two countries that are also members of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> the AU <a href="/wiki/Peace_and_Security_Council" title="Peace and Security Council">Peace and Security Council</a> voted on 26 August 2011 not to recognise it, insisting that a ceasefire be agreed to and a national <a href="/wiki/Unity_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Unity government">unity government</a> be formed by both sides in the civil war.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> A number of AU member states led by <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a> requested that the AU recognise the <a href="/wiki/National_Transitional_Council" title="National Transitional Council">NTC</a> as Libya's interim governing authority,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> and several other AU member states have recognised the <a href="/wiki/National_Transitional_Council" title="National Transitional Council">NTC</a> regardless of the Peace and Security Council's decision.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> However, AU member states <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> have indicated they will not recognise the <a href="/wiki/National_Transitional_Council" title="National Transitional Council">NTC</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> has expressed reservations as well.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 September 2011, the African Union officially recognised the <a href="/wiki/National_Transitional_Council" title="National Transitional Council">National Transitional Council</a> as the legitimate representative of <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In post-Gaddafi Libya, the African Union believes it still has an important responsibility to the country despite its failure to contribute to the conflict when it originated. The AU is essentially fighting an uphill battle though because of their failure to support the Libyan rebels. Although the African Union is there to keep peace, it is not a long term solution. The goal, as stated by the AU, is to establish a Libyan government that is sustainable to ensuring the peace in Libya. To achieve some level of peace in Libya, the AU has to moderate peace talks which are aimed at achieving compromises and power sharing accommodations as well.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Togo">Togo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Togo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In response to the death of <a href="/wiki/Gnassingb%C3%A9_Eyad%C3%A9ma" title="Gnassingbé Eyadéma">Gnassingbé Eyadéma</a>, President of <a href="/wiki/Togo" title="Togo">Togo</a>, on 5 February 2005, AU leaders described the naming of his son <a href="/wiki/Faure_Gnassingb%C3%A9" title="Faure Gnassingbé">Faure Gnassingbé</a> the successor as a <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d&#39;état">military coup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Togo's constitution calls for the speaker of parliament to succeed the president in the event of his death. By law, the parliament speaker must call national elections to choose a new president within sixty days. The AU's protest forced Gnassingbé to hold elections. Under heavy allegations of election fraud, he was officially elected President on 4 May 2005.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mauritania">Mauritania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Mauritania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 3 August 2005, a coup in <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a> led the African Union to suspend the country from all organisational activities. The Military Council that took control of Mauritania promised to hold elections within two years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> These were held in early 2007, the first time that the country had held elections that were generally agreed to be of an acceptable standard. Following the elections, Mauritania's membership of the AU was restored. However, on 6 August 2008, a fresh coup overthrew the government elected in 2007. The AU once again suspended Mauritania from the continental body.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The suspension was once again lifted in 2009 after the military junta agreed with the opposition to organise elections.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mali">Mali</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Mali">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Malian army was formed on 1 October 1960 and was supported by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> In March 2012, a military coup was staged in Mali, when an alliance of Touareg and Islamist forces conquered the north, resulting in a coming to power of the Islamists. This resulted in the deaths of hundreds of Malian soldiers and the loss of control over their camps and positions.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> After a military intervention with help from French troops, the region was in control of the Malian army. To reinstall local authorities, the AU helped to form a caretaker government, supporting it and holding presidential elections in Mali in July 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-dandc.eu_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dandc.eu-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, a summit for the African Union was held and it was decided that the African Union was going to enlarge their military presence in Mali. The AU decided to do this because of increasing tensions between al-Qaeda forces and the Mali army. There have been several rebel groups that are vying for control of parts of Mali. These rebel groups include the <a href="/wiki/National_Movement_for_the_Liberation_of_Azawad" title="National Movement for the Liberation of Azawad">National Movement for the Liberation of Azawad (MNLA)</a>, the National Front for the Liberation of Azawad (FLNA), Ganda Koy, Ganda Izo, <a href="/wiki/Ansar_al-Din_Front" title="Ansar al-Din Front">Ansar ad-Din</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">Al-Qaeda</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda_in_the_Islamic_Maghreb" title="Al-Qaeda in the Islamic Maghreb">Islamic Maghreb (AQIM)</a>. AU forces have been tasked with counterinsurgency missions in Mali as well as governing presidential elections to ensure as smooth a transition of power as possible.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_conflicts_and_peacekeeping">Regional conflicts and peacekeeping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Regional conflicts and peacekeeping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>One of the objectives of the AU is to "promote peace, security, and stability on the continent".<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> Among its principles is "Peaceful resolution of conflicts among Member States of the Union through such appropriate means as may be decided upon by the Assembly".<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> The primary body charged with implementing these objectives and principles is the Peace and Security Council. The PSC has the power, among other things, to authorise peace support missions, to impose sanctions in case of unconstitutional change of government, and to "take initiatives and action it deems appropriate" in response to potential or actual conflicts. The PSC is a decision-making body in its own right, and its decisions are binding on member states.
</p><p>Article 4(h) of the Constitutive Act, repeated in article 4 of the Protocol to the Constitutive Act on the PSC, also recognises the right of the Union to intervene in member state in circumstances of war crimes, genocide and crimes against humanity. Any decision to intervene in a member state under article 4 of the Constitutive Act will be made by the Assembly on the recommendation of the PSC.
</p><p>Since it first met in 2004, the PSC has been active in relation to the crises in Darfur, Comoros, Somalia, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Republic of Congo">Democratic Republic of Congo</a>, Burundi, Côte d'Ivoire and other countries. It has adopted resolutions creating the AU peacekeeping operations in Somalia and Darfur, and imposing sanctions against persons undermining peace and security (such as travel bans and asset freezes against the leaders of the rebellion in Comoros). The Council is in the process of overseeing the establishment of a "standby force" to serve as a permanent African peacekeeping force.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Institute for Security Studies, South Africa, March 2008.
</p><p>The founding treaty of the AU also called for the establishment of the African Peace and Security Architecture (APSA), including the <a href="/wiki/African_Standby_Force" title="African Standby Force">African Standby Force</a> (ASF), which is to be deployed in emergencies. That means, in cases of genocide or other serious human-rights violations, an ASF mission can be launched even against the wishes of the government of the country concerned, as long as it is approved by the AU General Assembly. In the past AU peacekeeping missions, the concept was not yet applied, forces had to be mobilised from member states. The AU is planning on putting the concept into practise by 2015 at the earliest.<sup id="cite_ref-dandc.eu_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dandc.eu-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="Was this done? If not, how did the plans change? (July 2018)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Darfur.2C_Sudan"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Darfur,_Sudan">Darfur, Sudan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Darfur, Sudan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/African_Union_Mission_in_Sudan" title="African Union Mission in Sudan">African Union Mission in Sudan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eritrea_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Eritrea_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/220px-Eritrea_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Eritrea_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/330px-Eritrea_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Eritrea_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/440px-Eritrea_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="450" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eritrea_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/South_Sudanese_independence_referendum,_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="South Sudanese independence referendum, 2011">South Sudanese independence referendum, 2011</a></div></div></div>
<p>In response to the ongoing <a href="/wiki/Darfur_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Darfur conflict">Darfur conflict</a> in Sudan, the AU has deployed 7,000 peacekeepers, many from Rwanda and Nigeria, to <a href="/wiki/Darfur" title="Darfur">Darfur</a>. While a donor's conference in Addis Ababa in 2005 helped raise funds to sustain the peacekeepers through that year and into 2006, in July 2006 the AU said it would pull out at the end of September when its mandate expires.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Critics of the AU peacekeepers, including Dr. <a href="/wiki/Eric_Reeves" title="Eric Reeves">Eric Reeves</a>, have said these forces are largely ineffective due to lack of funds, personnel, and expertise. Monitoring an area roughly the size of France has made it even more difficult to sustain an effective mission. In June 2006, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a> appropriated US$173&#160;million for the AU force. Some, such as the <a href="/wiki/Genocide_Intervention_Network" title="Genocide Intervention Network">Genocide Intervention Network</a>, have called for UN or <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> intervention to augment and/or replace the AU peacekeepers. The UN has considered deploying a force, though it would not likely enter the country until at least October 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The under-funded and badly equipped AU mission was set to expire on 31 December 2006 but was extended to 30 June 2007 and merged with the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_African_Union_Mission_in_Darfur" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations African Union Mission in Darfur">United Nations African Union Mission in Darfur</a> in October 2007. In July 2009 the African Union ceased cooperation with the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a>, refusing to recognise the international arrest warrant it had issued against Sudan's leader, <a href="/wiki/Omar_al-Bashir" title="Omar al-Bashir">Omar al-Bashir</a>, who was indicted in 2008 for <a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">war crimes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The AU struggled to have a strategic role in the independence talks and the reconciliation process of <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, due to overwhelming interests of African and non-African powers, its influence is still limited and not consistent.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Somalia">Somalia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Somalia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/African_Union_Mission_to_Somalia" class="mw-redirect" title="African Union Mission to Somalia">African Union Mission to Somalia</a></div>
<p>From the early 1990s up until 2000, <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> was without a functioning central government. A peace agreement aimed at ending the <a href="/wiki/Somali_Civil_War" title="Somali Civil War">civil war</a> that broke out following the collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Siad_Barre" title="Siad Barre">Siad Barre</a> regime was signed in 2006 after many years of peace talks. However, the new government was almost immediately threatened by further violence. In February 2007, the African Union (AU) and European Union (EU) worked together to establish the <a href="/wiki/African_Union_Mission_to_Somalia_(2007-present)" class="mw-redirect" title="African Union Mission to Somalia (2007-present)">African Union Mission in Somalia (AMISOM)</a>. The purpose of AMISOM was to create a foundation that would hopefully provide aid to some of Somalia's most vulnerable and keep the peace in the region. They are tasked with everything from protecting federal institutions to facilitating humanitarian relief operations. Much of the AU's opposition comes from an Islamic extremist group named <a href="/wiki/Al-Shabaab_(militant_group)" title="Al-Shabaab (militant group)">al-Shabaab</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> To temporarily shore up the government's military base, starting in March 2007, AU soldiers began arriving in <a href="/wiki/Mogadishu" title="Mogadishu">Mogadishu</a> as part of a peacekeeping force that was intended by the AU to eventually be 8,000 strong.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Eritrea recalled its ambassadors to the African Union on 20 November 2009<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> after the African Union called on the United Nations Security Council to impose sanctions on them due to their alleged support of Somali Islamists attempting to topple the <a href="/wiki/Transitional_Federal_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Transitional Federal Government">Transitional Federal Government</a> of Somalia, the internationally recognised government of Somalia which holds Somalia's seat on the African Union.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> On 22 December 2009, the United Nations Security Council passed <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1907" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1907">UNSCR 1907</a>, which imposed an arms embargo on Eritrea, travel bans on Eritrean leaders, and asset freezes on Eritrean officials. Eritrea strongly criticised the resolution. In January 2011, Eritrea reestablished their mission to the AU in Addis Ababa.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the fall of 2011, AMISOM forces, along with Kenyan and Ethiopian forces launched a set of offensive attacks on the <a href="/wiki/Al-Shabaab_(militant_group)" title="Al-Shabaab (militant group)">al-Shabaab</a>. In these attacks, <a href="/wiki/African_Union_Mission_to_Somalia_(2007-present)" class="mw-redirect" title="African Union Mission to Somalia (2007-present)">AMISOM</a> forces were able to reclaim key cities including the Somali capital of <a href="/wiki/Mogadishu" title="Mogadishu">Mogadishu</a>. In September 2013, Ethan Bueno de Mesquita, a political scientist, argued that with the help of <a href="/wiki/African_Union_Mission_to_Somalia_(2007-present)" class="mw-redirect" title="African Union Mission to Somalia (2007-present)">AMISOM</a> forces, they had made it “nearly impossible for <a href="/wiki/Al-Shabaab_(militant_group)" title="Al-Shabaab (militant group)">al-Shabaab</a> to hold territory even in its former strongholds in southern Somalia”. Although lots of progress has been made towards peace in the region, it should still be noted that African Union forces’ still get attacked regularly. Despite <a href="/wiki/African_Union_Mission_to_Somalia_(2007-present)" class="mw-redirect" title="African Union Mission to Somalia (2007-present)">AMISOM</a> being effective, it is vastly underfunded and many forces lack the resources required. Funding for humanitarian relief and the formation of armies tends to be vastly undercut.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Anjouan.2C_Comoros"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Anjouan,_Comoros">Anjouan, Comoros</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Anjouan, Comoros">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2008_invasion_of_Anjouan" title="2008 invasion of Anjouan">2008 invasion of Anjouan</a></div>
<p>A successful 2008 invasion of <a href="/wiki/Anjouan" title="Anjouan">Anjouan</a> by AU and <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">Comoros</a> forces to stop self-declared president <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Bacar" title="Mohamed Bacar">Mohamed Bacar</a>, whose 2007 re-election was declared illegal.<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Prior to the invasion, France helped transport Tanzanian troops but their position in the disagreement was questioned when a French police helicopter was suspected of attempting to sneak Bacar into French exile.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> The first wave of troops landed on Anjouan Bay on 25 March and soon took over the airfield in <a href="/wiki/Ouani" title="Ouani">Ouani</a>, ultimately aiming to locate and remove Bacar from office.<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> On the same day, the airport, capital, and second city were overrun and the presidential palace was deserted.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Bacar escaped and sought asylum in France and the government of Comoros demanded they return him so they may determine his consequence.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Many of Bacar's primary supporters were arrested by the end of March, including <a href="/wiki/Caabi_El-Yachroutu_Mohamed" title="Caabi El-Yachroutu Mohamed">Caabi El-Yachroutu Mohamed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Halidi" title="Ibrahim Halidi">Ibrahim Halidi</a>. His asylum request was rejected in 15 May as France agreed to cooperate with the Comoran governments demand.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> His presidential position was then occupied by <a href="/wiki/Moussa_Toybou" title="Moussa Toybou">Moussa Toybou</a> after winning the election in 29 June.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 20em; -webkit-column-width: 20em; column-width: 20em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/17th_Ordinary_African_Union_Summit" title="17th Ordinary African Union Summit">17th Ordinary African Union Summit</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/African_Century" class="mw-redirect" title="African Century">African Century</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/African_Renaissance" title="African Renaissance">African Renaissance</a></li>

<div role="navigation" class="navbox" aria-labelledby="Pan-Africanism_border&amp;#124;30px" style="padding:3px"><table class="nowraplinks mw-collapsible autocollapse navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit"><tbody><tr><th scope="col" class="navbox-title" colspan="2"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Pan-Africanism" title="Template:Pan-Africanism"><abbr title="View this template" style=";;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none;
